The compiler handles:\\n- Lexical analysis: identifying keywords, functions, operators, and cell references\\n- Syntax validation: ensuring the formula follows the correct grammar\\n- Token creation: converting parsed elements into FormulaToken objects\\n- The compiled tokens are stored in a ScTokenArray (sc/inc/tokenarray.hxx)\\n\\nKey methods:\\n- ScCompiler::CompileTokenArray() - main compilation entry point\\n- ScCompiler::CompileFormula() - parses formula string\\n\\n## 2. Formula Cell Storage (sc/inc/formulacell.hxx and sc/source/core/data/formulacell.cxx)\\nScFormulaCell is the cell type that holds:\\n- A ScTokenArray (pCode) - the compiled token array\\n- A ScFormulaResult (aResult) - the cached formula result\\n- Dirty flags (bDirty, bCompile) - indicating whether recalculation is needed\\n- Interpreter state tracking for circular references\\n\\nKey methods:\\n- ScFormulaCell::Interpret() - triggers formula evaluation\\n- ScFormulaCell::InterpretTail() - core interpretation logic\\n- ScFormulaCell::SetDirty() - marks cell for recalculation\\n- ScFormulaCell::MaybeInterpret() - lazy evaluation trigger\\n\\n## 3. Formula Evaluation/Interpretation (sc/source/core/inc/interpre.hxx and sc/source/core/tool/interpr*.cxx)\\nThe ScInterpreter class is the bytecode interpreter that evaluates compiled formulas:\\n- Maintains evaluation state: the parameter stack, current position in token array\\n- Implements opcodes: functions (SUM, AVERAGE, etc.), operators (+, -, *, /), and references\\n- Manages array formulas and matrix operations\\n- Handles function calls: both built-in and external functions\\n\\nThe interpreter is split across multiple files:\\n- interpr1.cxx (~435KB) - basic arithmetic, references, and fundamental operations\\n- interpr2.cxx - string functions and conditional logic\\n- interpr3.cxx - mathematical and statistical functions\\n- interpr4.cxx - financial, date/time, and database functions\\n- interpr5.cxx - array operations and additional functions\\n\\nKey methods:\\n- ScInterpreter::Interpret() - main evaluation entry point\\n- Formula token iterator iterates through the compiled token array\\n- Each opcode triggers the appropriate evaluation function\\n\\n## 4. Recalculation Scheduling (sc/source/core/data/formulacell.cxx)\\nRecalculation is managed through:\\n- SetDirty() - marks formulas and their dependents as needing recalculation\\n- Dirty flags on ScFormulaCell control when evaluation occurs\\n- The formula's recalculation mode (stored in ScTokenArray, inherited from formula::FormulaTokenArray):\\n  - NORMAL: standard automatic recalculation\\n  - ALWAYS: volatile functions (NOW, RAND) always recalculate\\n  - ONLOAD: recalculate when document is loaded\\n  - FORCED: force recalculation\\n\\n## 5. Token Management (sc/source/core/tool/token.cxx and sc/inc/token.hxx)\\nSpecialized token classes handle different reference types:\\n- ScSingleRefToken - single cell reference (e.g., A1)\\n- ScDoubleRefToken - range reference (e.g., A1:A10)\\n- ScMatrixToken - inline array literals\\n- ScExternalSingleRefToken - references to external documents\\n- ScExternalDoubleRefToken - range references to external documents\\n\\n## Evaluation Flow\\nFor a formula like \\\"=SUM(A1:A10)\\\":\\n1. ScCompiler parses \\\"SUM\\\", \\\"(\\\", \\\"A1:A10\\\", \\\")\\\" into tokens (opcode for SUM, range reference)\\n2. ScFormulaCell stores this in pCode (ScTokenArray)\\n3. On recalculation, ScFormulaCell::Interpret() creates a ScInterpreter\\n4. ScInterpreter iterates through tokens, evaluating operands and executing opcodes\\n5. The SUM opcode handler iterates through A1:A10, summing the values\\n6. Result is cached in ScFormulaCell::aResult and returned\\n7. Cell dependents are marked dirty through SetDirty() for cascade updates\"\n    31→}\n    32→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware.
